# API Call Chain: Grafana to Loki Query Path

## Your Task

Identify the key types/functions at each hop in this HTTP call chain: 1. In `grafana/grafana`: What is the type/struct that acts as the HTTP client for Loki queries? 2. In `sg-evals/grafana-loki`: What is the function that parses incoming HTTP instant query requests?

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

    45→
    46→func makeDataRequest(ctx context.Context, lokiDsUrl string, query lokiQuery) (*http.Request, error) {
    47→	qs := url.Values{}
    48→	qs.Set("query", query.Expr)
    49→
    50→	qs.Set("direction", string(query.Direction))
    51→
    52→	// MaxLines defaults to zero when not received,
    53→	// and Loki does not like limit=0, even when it is not needed
    54→	// (for example for metric queries), so we
    55→	// only send it when it's set
    56→	if query.MaxLines > 0 {
    57→		qs.Set("limit", fmt.Sprintf("%d", query.MaxLines))
    58→	}

    57→		qs.Set("limit", fmt.Sprintf("%d", query.MaxLines))
    58→	}

    34→func interpolateVariables(expr string, interval time.Duration, timeRange time.Duration, queryType dataquery.LokiQueryType, step time.Duration) string {
    35→	intervalText := gtime.FormatInterval(interval)
    36→	stepText := gtime.FormatInterval(step)
    37→	intervalMsText := strconv.FormatInt(int64(interval/time.Millisecond), 10)
    38→
    39→	rangeMs := timeRange.Milliseconds()
    40→	rangeSRounded := int64(math.Round(float64(rangeMs) / 1000.0))
    41→	rangeMsText := strconv.FormatInt(rangeMs, 10)
    42→	rangeSText := strconv.FormatInt(rangeSRounded, 10)
    43→
    44→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varIntervalMs, intervalMsText)
    45→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varInterval, intervalText)
    46→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varRangeMs, rangeMsText)
    47→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varRangeS, rangeSText)
    48→	ex

    34→func interpolateVariables(expr string, interval time.Duration, timeRange time.Duration, queryType dataquery.LokiQueryType, step time.Duration) string {

    36→	stepText := gtime.FormatInterval(step)

    38→
    39→	rangeMs := timeRange.Milliseconds()
    40→	rangeSRounded := int64(math.Round(float64(rangeMs) / 1000.0))
    41→	rangeMsText := strconv.FormatInt(rangeMs, 10)
    42→	rangeSText := strconv.FormatInt(rangeSRounded, 10)
    43→
    44→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varIntervalMs, intervalMsText)
    45→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varInterval, intervalText)
    46→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varRangeMs, rangeMsText)
    47→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varRangeS, rangeSText)

    46→func makeDataRequest(ctx context.Context, lokiDsUrl string, query lokiQuery) (*http.Request, error) {
    47→	qs := url.Values{}
    48→	qs.Set("query", query.Expr)
    49→
    50→	qs.Set("direction", string(query.Direction))
    51→
    52→	// MaxLines defaults to zero when not received,
    53→	// and Loki does not like limit=0, even when it is not needed
    54→	// (for example for metric queries), so we
    55→	// only send it when it's set
    56→	if query.MaxLines > 0 {
    57→		qs.Set("limit", fmt.Sprintf("%d", query.MaxLines))
    58→	}
    59→
    60→	lokiUrl, err := url.Parse(lokiDsUrl)
    61→	if err != nil {
    62→		return nil, backend.DownstreamError(fmt.Errorf("failed to parse Loki URL: %w", err))
    63→	}
    64→
    65→	switch query.QueryType {
    66→	case QueryTypeRange:
    67→		{
    68→			qs.Set("start", strconv.FormatInt(query.Start.UnixNano(), 10))
    69→			qs.Set("end", strconv.FormatInt(query.End.UnixNano(), 10))
    70→			// NOTE: technically for streams-producing queries `step`
    71→			// is ignored, so it would be nicer to not send it in such cases,
    72→			// but we cannot detect that situation, so we always send it.
    73→			// it should not break anything.
    74→			// NOTE2: we do this at millisecond precision for two reasons:
    75→			//  a. Loki cannot do steps with better precision anyway,
    76→			//     so the microsecond & nanosecond part can be ignored.
    77→			//  b. having it always be number+'ms' makes it more robust and
    78→			//     precise, as Loki does not support step with float number
    79→			//     and time-specifier, like "1.5s"
    80→			qs.Set("step", fmt.Sprintf("%dms", query.Step.Milliseconds()))
    81→			lokiUrl.Path = path.Join(lokiUrl.Path, "/loki/api/v1/query_range")
    82→		}
    83→	ca

     1→package loki
     2→
     3→import (
     4→	"bytes"

     6→	"encoding/json"
     7→	"fmt"
     8→	"io"

    14→	"github.com/grafana/grafana-app-sdk/logging"
    15→)
    16→
    17→type Config struct {
    18→	ReadPathURL       *url.URL
    19→	WritePathURL      *url.URL
    20→	BasicAuthUser     string
    21→	BasicAuthPassword string
    22→	TenantID          string
    23→	ExternalLabels    map[string]string
    24→	MaxQuerySize      int
    25→}
    26→
    27→type Stream struct {
    28→	Stream map[string]string `json:"stream"`
    29→	Values []Sample          `json:"values"`
    30→}
    31→
    32→type Sample struct {
    33→	T time.Time
    34→	V string
    35→}
    36→
    37→func (r Sample) MarshalJSON() ([]byte, error) {
    38→	return json.Marshal([2]string{
    39→		fmt.Sprintf("%d", r.T.UnixNano()), r.V,
    40→	})
    41→}
    42→
    43→func (r *Sample) UnmarshalJSON(b []byte) error {
    44→	var tuple [2]string
    45→	if err := json.Unmarshal(b, &tuple); err != nil {
    46→		return fmt.Errorf("failed to deserialize sample in Loki response: %w", err)
    47→	}
    48→	nano, err := strconv.ParseInt(tuple[0], 10, 64)
    49→	if err != nil {
    50→		return fmt.Errorf("timestamp in Loki sample not convertible to nanosecond epoch: %v", tuple[0])
    51→	}
    52→	r.T = time.Unix(0, nano)

   150→	}
   151→	if err != nil {
   152→		return QueryRes{}, fmt.Errorf("error sending request: %w", err)

   157→		return QueryRes{}, fmt.Errorf("error reading request response: %w", err)
   158→	}
   159→
   160→	if res.StatusCode < 200 || res.StatusCode >= 300 {
   161→		if len(body) > 0 {
   162→			log.Error("Error response from Loki", "response", string(body), "status", res.StatusCode)
   163→		} else {
   164→			log.Error("Error response from Loki with an empty body", "status", res.StatusCode)
   165→		}
   166→		return QueryRes{}, fmt.Errorf("received a non-200 response from loki, status: %d", res.StatusCode)
   167→	}
   168→
   169→	var queryRes QueryRes
   170→	if err := json.Unmarshal(body, &queryRes); err != nil {
   171→		return QueryRes{}, fmt.Errorf("error unmarshaling loki response: %w", err)
   172→	}
   173→
   174→	log.Debug("Successfully queried Loki", "status", res.StatusCode, "streams", len(queryRes.Data.Result))
   175→	return queryRes, nil
   176→}

    34→func interpolateVariables(expr string, interval time.Duration, timeRange time.Duration, queryType dataquery.LokiQueryType, step time.Duration) string {

    41→	rangeMsText := strconv.FormatInt(rangeMs, 10)
    42→	rangeSText := strconv.FormatInt(rangeSRounded, 10)
    43→
    44→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varIntervalMs, intervalMsText)
    45→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varInterval, intervalText)
    46→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varRangeMs, rangeMsText)

Perfect! I've created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`. Let me verify the content is complete and accurate:

## Summary of Findings:

**Question 1: HTTP Client Type in Grafana for Loki Queries**
- **Answer**: The `LokiAPI` struct (located in `pkg/tsdb/loki/api.go`, lines 29-34)
- This struct wraps an `*http.Client` and contains fields for URL, logger, and tracer
- It's instantiated via the `newLokiAPI()` function

**Question 2: Function that Parses Incoming HTTP Instant Query Requests in Loki**
- **Answer**: `QueryHandler` function in `pkg/querier/http/handler.go` (in grafana/loki repository)
- This is the HTTP handler for the `/loki/api/v1/query` endpoint
- It extracts and processes the `query` parameter (LogQL expression) and `time` parameter

**The Complete Call Chain:**
1. Grafana: `QueryData()` receives the query request
2. Grafana: `parseQuery()` determines it's an instant query
3. Grafana: `makeDataRequest()` constructs the HTTP GET request to `/loki/api/v1/query`
4. Grafana: `LokiAPI.DataQuery()` executes the HTTP request
5. Loki: `QueryHandler()` receives and parses the instant query request

The answer file includes:
- **files**: List of relevant source files from both repositories
- **symbols**: Key types and functions identified in the call chain
- **chain**: The sequential flow of the API call chain
- **text**: Detailed narrative explanation with code locations and line numbers

prometheus.NewCounterVec(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n\t\tNamespace: \"promtail\",\n\t\tName:      \"dropped_entries_total\",\n\t\tHelp:      \"Number of log entries dropped because failed to be sent to \"request_duration_seconds\",\n\t\tHelp:      \"Duration of send requests.\",\n\t}, []string{\"status_code\", HostLabel})\n\tm.batchRetries = prometheus.NewCounterVec(prometheus.CounterOpts{\n\t\tNamespace: \"promtail\",\n\t\tName:      \"batch_retries_total\",\n\t\tHelp:      \"Number of times batches has had to be retried.\",\n\t}, m.batchRetries).(*prometheus.CounterVec)\n\t}\n\n\treturn &m\n}\n\nfunc mustRegisterOrGet(reg prometheus.Registerer, c prometheus.Collector) prometheus.Collector {\n\tif err := reg.Register(c); err != nil {\n\t\tpromError := prometheus.AlreadyRegisteredError{}\n\t\tif errors.As(err, &promError) {\n\t\t\treturn promError.ExistingCollector\n\t\t}\n\t\tpanic(err)\n\t}\n\treturn c\n}\n\n// Client pushes entries to Loki and can be stopped\ntype Client interface {\n\tChan() chan<- Entry\n\n\tStop()\n\tStopNow()\n}\n\n// Client for pushing logs in snappy-compressed protos over HTTP.\ntype client struct {\n\tmetrics *metrics\n\tlogger  log.Logger\n\tcfg     Config\n\tclient  *http.Client\n\tentries chan Entry\n\n\tonce sync.Once\n\twg   sync.WaitGroup\n\n\t// ctx is used in any upstream calls new Client.\nfunc New(reg prometheus.Registerer, cfg Config, logger log.Logger) (Client, error) {\n\treturn newClient(reg, cfg, logger)\n}\n\nfunc newClient(reg prometheus.Registerer, cfg Config, counter := range c.metrics.countersWithHost {\n\t\tcounter.WithLabelValues(c.cfg.URL.Host).Add(0)\n\t}\n\n\tc.wg.Add(1)\n\tgo c.run()\n\treturn c, nil\n}\n\n// NewWithTripperware creates a new Loki client with a custom tripperware.\nfunc NewWithTripperware(reg prometheus.Registerer, cfg Config, logger log.Logger, tp Tripperware) (Client, error) {\n\tc, err := newClient(reg, cfg, logger)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\tif tp != nil {\n\t\tc.client.Transport = tp(c.client.Transport)\n\t}\n\n\treturn c, nil\n}\n\nfunc (c *client) run() {\n\tbatches := map[string]*batch{}\n\n\t// Given the client handles multiple batches (1 per tenant) and each batch\n\t// can be created at a different point in time, we look for batches whose\n\t// max wait time has been reached every 10 times per BatchWait, so that the\n\t// maximum delay we have sending batches is 10% of the max waiting time.\n\t// We apply a cap of 10ms to the ticker, to avoid too frequent checks in\n\t// case the BatchWait is very low.\n\tminWaitCheckFrequency := 10 * time.Millisecond\n\tmaxWaitCheckFrequency := c.cfg.BatchWait / 10\n\tif maxWaitCheckFrequency < minWaitCheckFrequency {\n\t\tmaxWaitCheckFrequency = minWaitCheckFrequency\n\t}\n\n\tmaxWaitCheck := time.NewTicker(maxWaitCheckFrequency)\n\n\tdefer func() {\n\t\tmaxWaitCheck.Stop()\n\t\t// Send all pending batches\n\t\tfor tenantID, batch := range batches {\n\t\t\tc.sendBatch(tenantID, batch)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tc.wg.Done()\n\t}()\n\n\tfor {\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase e, ok := <-c.entries:\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\treturn\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\ttenantID := c.getTenantID(e.Labels)\n\t\t\tbatch, ok := batches[tenantID]\n\n\t\t\t// If the batch doesn't exist yet, we create a new one with the entry\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\tbatches[tenantID] = newBatch(e)\n\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// If adding the entry to the batch will increase the size over the max\n\t\t\t// size allowed, we do send the current batch and then create a new one\n\t\t\tif batch.sizeBytesAfter(e) > c.cfg.BatchSize {\n\t\t\t\tc.sendBatch(tenantID, batch)\n\n\t\t\t\tbatches[tenantID] = newBatch(e)\n\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// The max size of the batch isn't reached, so we can add the entry\n\t\t\tbatch.add(e)\n\n\t\tcase <-maxWaitCheck.C:\n\t\t\t// Send all batches whose max wait time has been reached\n\t\t\tfor tenantID, batch := range batches {\n\t\t\t\tif batch.age() < c.cfg.BatchWait {\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t\tc.sendBatch(tenantID, batch)\n\t\t\t\tdelete(batches, tenantID)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (c *client) getTenantID(labels model.LabelSet) string {\n\t// Check if it has been overridden while processing the pipeline stages\n\tif value, ok := labels[ReservedLabelTenantID]; ok {\n\t\treturn string(value)\n\t}\n\n\t// Check if has been specified in the config\n\tif c.cfg.TenantID != \"\" {\n\t\treturn c.cfg.TenantID\n\t}\n\n\t// Defaults to an empty string, which means the X-Scope-OrgID header\n\t// will not be sent\n\treturn \"\"\n}\n\nfunc (c *client) Chan() chan<- Entry {\n\treturn c.entries\n}\n\nfunc (c *client) sendBatch(tenantID string, batch *batch) {\n\tbuf, entriesCount, err := batch.encode()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tc.logger.Error(\"error encoding batch\", \"error\", err)\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tbufBytes := float64(len(buf))\n\tc.metrics.encodedBytes.WithLabelValues(c.cfg.URL.Host).Add(bufBytes)\n\n\tbackoff := backoff.New(c.ctx, c.cfg.BackoffConfig)\n\tvar status int\n\tfor {\n\t\tstart := time.Now()\n\t\t// send uses `timeout` internally, so `context.Background` is good enough.\n\t\tstatus, err = c.send(context.Background(), tenantID, buf)\n\n\t\tc.metrics.requestDuration.WithLabelValues(strconv.Itoa(status), c.cfg.URL.Host).Observe(time.Since(start).Seconds())\n\n\t\t// Only retry 429s, 500s and connection-level errors.\n\t\tif status > 0 && status != 429 && status/100 != 5 {\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tc.logger.Warn(\"error sending batch, will retry\", \"status\", status, \"error\", err)\n\t\tc.metrics.batchRetries.WithLabelValues(c.cfg.URL.Host).Inc()\n\t\tbackoff.Wait()\n\n\t\t// Make sure it sends at least once before checking for retry.\n\t\tif !backoff.Ongoing() {\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tc.logger.Error(\"final error sending batch\", \"status\", status)\n\t\tc.metrics.droppedBytes.WithLabelValues(c.cfg.URL.Host).Add(bufBytes)\n\t\tc.metrics.droppedEntries.WithLabelValues(c.cfg.URL.Host).Add(float64(entriesCount))\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (c *client) tenantID)\n\t}\n\n\tresp, err := c.client.Do(req)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn -1, err\n\t}\n\tdefer func() {\n\t\terr := resp.Body.Close()\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tc.logger.Error(\"failed to close the response body\", \"error\", err)\n\t\t}\n\t}()\n\n\tif resp.StatusCode/100 != 2 {\n\t\tscanner := bufio.NewScanner(io.LimitReader(resp.Body, maxErrMsgLen))\n\t\tline := \"\"\n\t\tif scanner.Scan() {\n\t\t\tline = scanner.Text()\n\t\t}\n\t\terr = fmt.Errorf(\"server returned HTTP status %s (%d): %s\", resp.Status, resp.StatusCode, line)\n\t}\n\treturn resp.StatusCode, err\n}\n\n// Stop the client.\nfunc (c *client) Stop() {\n\tc.once.Do(func() { close(c.entries) })\n\tc.wg.Wait()\n}\n\n// StopNow stops the client without retries\nfunc (c *client) StopNow() {\n\t// cancel will stop retrying http requests.\n\tc.cancel()\n\tc.Stop()\n}\n",
